<div id="review_1585365651" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1585365651" />
    <a title="Mandy Radley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28892382-mandy-radley"><img alt="Mandy Radley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482720088p2/28892382.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1585365651?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mandy Radley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mandy Radley" href="/user/show/28892382-mandy-radley">Mandy Radley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1585365651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3320608670365044541">4.5 stars<br/>Max born on 20 April 1936 (Hitler's birthday) the first born in the Lebensborn programme designed to produce the Aryan race, he doesn't know his mother or father only that his mother was impregnated by a German SS officer. Baptised by Hitler he becomes the role model for all the other children. When he's 5 he helps the Germans kidnap Polish children and then meets and befriends Lukas a Polish Jew, blond, blue eyes who infiltrates the German's experiment for the perfect race. I enjoyed t</span>
  <span id="freeText3320608670365044541" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br />Max born on 20 April 1936 (Hitler's birthday) the first born in the Lebensborn programme designed to produce the Aryan race, he doesn't know his mother or father only that his mother was impregnated by a German SS officer. Baptised by Hitler he becomes the role model for all the other children. When he's 5 he helps the Germans kidnap Polish children and then meets and befriends Lukas a Polish Jew, blond, blue eyes who infiltrates the German's experiment for the perfect race. I enjoyed this book, but by no means is it a pleasant read, obviously with what the Germans did. The only downside and the reason I didn't give it 5 stars is that the story is told at the beginning by Max who is still a foetus and when the war is over is still only 9 years old. Realistically a child of this age and younger would not comprehend, speak, act as Max did in the book. So when reading the book I just had to try and forget that Max was an infant and just go with the story.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3320608670365044541" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12451706780758831900" style="display:none">A brilliant read from start to finish.     <div class="elementListBrownSeparator"></div>



  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1981925739" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1981925739" />
    <a title="Justin Williams" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18046843-justin-williams"><img alt="Justin Williams" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362863845p2/18046843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1981925739?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin Williams" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin Williams" href="/user/show/18046843-justin-williams">Justin Williams</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1981925739" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17540630878052209545">This is a book that NEEDS to be in every library. I knew about the Hitler Youth movement in Germany during World War II, but I had no idea about the horror of the Lebensborn ("Fountain of Life") programs. In an attempt to breed the perfect Aryan soldier, the Nazis would match S.S. Officers only with the bluest of eyes and blondest of hair with women of the same nordic qualities. If the baby didn't match with predetermined standards, they were "purified"...you guessed it, killed. <br/><br/>Not for the youn</span>
  <span id="freeText17540630878052209545" style="display:none">This is a book that NEEDS to be in every library. I knew about the Hitler Youth movement in Germany during World War II, but I had no idea about the horror of the Lebensborn ("Fountain of Life") programs. In an attempt to breed the perfect Aryan soldier, the Nazis would match S.S. Officers only with the bluest of eyes and blondest of hair with women of the same nordic qualities. If the baby didn't match with predetermined standards, they were "purified"...you guessed it, killed. <br /><br />Not for the youngest of children, I can see this book being challenged as soon as it hits the Young Adult shelves, but it's worth every second its on the shelf and every time its checked out. When starting, everything about the story makes you want to stop reading. Your feelings may tell you to close the book. Even the cover makes you want to avert your eyes at first glance. But this novel is important. It's sometimes good to feel uncomfortable, lonely, sad or insulted. Max will make you feel this way, but on finishing, you will be glad you made it through.<br /><br />***SPOILERS AHEAD***<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Max, by Sarah Cohen-Scali, follows Konrad von Kebnersol as a foul-mouthed, Nazi indoctrinated fetus, to his birth on the Fuhrer's birthday (signaling the second coming to the Nazi party of one of the scariest human beings to every walk the earth), to the end of World War II in a bombed out Berlin. The reader watches Konrad as he grows up under the ever-present eye of the brutal Dr. Ebner, is used as bait by the Braune Schwestern (Brown Sisters) to kidnap Polish children for Nazi brainwashing, befriends a Polish Jew, and survives the destruction of the Russian occupied Berlin after Hitler's suicide. <br /><br />This is one of those books I'm likely never to forget. Konrad is not a like-able character. He's detestable, at least at the very beginning. The book makes you want to cry and never laugh. The tone is dark, menacing. The reader witnesses the terror of the Nazi party through Konrad's eyes. Through childish innocence, the Nazi flags seem grand even to our own minds as the narrator sees them for the first time. This may remind us of our own childlike patriotism as we look at our flag unstained by visions of war. As Konrad grows, so do we. The once glimmering Nazi badges once-coveted by him as a child, become blemished, changing from a badge of honor to a badge of brutality before our very eyes as the protagonist is shown what a totalitarian regime looks like from the inside. But what does he know? In turn, what do we know looking through his eyes? Given a steel-barred cradle at birth, the cold violence inflicted upon he and his friends growing up in a school for German youth is the norm. It's not until Konrad meets Lukas, a Polish boy kidnapped by the Nazis in an effort to enlist more youth into their ranks, that he begins to understand that he, the perfect Aryan-bred soldier, is only human like everyone else. Lukas is Jewish, but he becomes a brother to Konrad and life is turned upside down. Jews are no longer the big-nosed, dark haired, clawed monsters of Nazi myth. Some have blond hair and blue eyes . Jews are no longer the monsters who steal away German children from their beds at night. Some are brotherly. But what can Konrad do? From birth he was taught Nazi lies. He was taught to hate Jews with unthinking malice. The Lebensborn program created automatons, but as we can see from Konrad's story, free thought still shines through.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17540630878052209545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2126775398" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2126775398" />
    <a title="Shoti" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53373701-shoti"><img alt="Shoti" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477072777p2/53373701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2126775398?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shoti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shoti" href="/user/show/53373701-shoti">Shoti</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53373701-shoti?shelf=fiction-ww2">fiction-ww2</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53373701-shoti?shelf=read-in-french">read-in-french</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2126775398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16542078138690263326"><i>Lebensborn</i> was a Nazi program launched in 1933 with the ambitious goal of breeding perfect, racially pure Aryan <i>Übermenschen</i> who could populate the newly conquered territories of German <i>Lebensraum</i> in the East. The program’s main ideologist and promoter was Heinrich Himmler, one of the sickest mind, in the face of a stiff competition, within the Nazi leadership. Lebensborn was organized and administered with meticulous precision as if it was an engineering project with a few technical challenges </span>
  <span id="freeText16542078138690263326" style="display:none"><i>Lebensborn</i> was a Nazi program launched in 1933 with the ambitious goal of breeding perfect, racially pure Aryan <i>Übermenschen</i> who could populate the newly conquered territories of German <i>Lebensraum</i> in the East. The program’s main ideologist and promoter was Heinrich Himmler, one of the sickest mind, in the face of a stiff competition, within the Nazi leadership. Lebensborn was organized and administered with meticulous precision as if it was an engineering project with a few technical challenges to be sorted out. Young females, chosen for their prominent Aryan characteristics, copulated with complete stranger SS officers, selected based on their equally notable Aryan properties. The newborns were separated from their mothers after a few months or, in other words, the mothers had to offer them to Deutschland and the Führer. There was no room for emotions here, Lebensborn was about programmed procreation, operating as a factory specialized in producing humans. The young received an immaculate Nazi indoctrination. When the number of homely grown babies turned out to be insufficient for the megalomaniac Nazi plans the program managers decided to start kidnapping thousands of Baltic, Polish, Ukrainian children who happened to have an Aryan enough appearance. The abducted children were sent to isolated special schools to learn German and get a thorough brainwash in Nazi ideology. In sum, every slice of Lebensborn is shrieking so hysterically and loudly from utter craziness that it serves as a fascinating topic for a novel.<br /><br />The novel follows the life of Max, the very first baby born under the auspices of Lebensborn, from 1936 to 1945. Max’s growing up coincides with different stages of corresponding German history, transpiring from euphoric Nazism through strenuous war efforts to total collapse and disillusion. The novel’s tone, in sync with the newborn / infant / toddler / child protagonist, is deliberately playful and humorous. That often creates a shocking and powerful contrast with the dreadful atrocities ongoing in the world. Despite the often cruel scenes, both emotional and physical, I consider the book best suits a YA audience. For its tone it could be a great read for an adolescent to help understand some of the craziness ongoing in this era. Unfortunately there is a fundamental flaw in the novel’s main presumption that kept bothering me. It’s fine that Max, born from a Nazi mother and a Nazi father, is a perfect prototype of the Aryan race with his pale blonde hair, piercing light blue eyes, etc. But, more than that, Max is also a devoted Nazi believer since the very first minute of his life. As if the genes could transfer not only physical characteristics but complete ideologies. The author might have chosen this as a convenient approach to depict an authentic Nazi perspective, through the eyes of Max, from the novel’s beginning. At the same time, this choice also relays the unfortunate message that parents may infuse immutable ideologies into their offspring - as if the concept underlying Lebensborn had ultimately been correct. Other than this glitch I liked the book and will recommend it to my two sons when they become 15-16 or so.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16542078138690263326" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15527032855366377183">Konrad van Kebnersol, called Max by his birth mother, is the product of Lebensborn, a secret Nazi breeding program designed to create an army of perfect Aryan children. Fully indoctrinated with Nazi propaganda since birth, Max has become a mascot of sorts for the Lebensborn program. As such, he acts as bait for the abduction of Polish children who could pass as Aryan. Once he is no longer viable bait, he is enrolled at the Kalish school to facilitate the Germinization of the abductees. There he </span>
  <span id="freeText15527032855366377183" style="display:none">Konrad van Kebnersol, called Max by his birth mother, is the product of Lebensborn, a secret Nazi breeding program designed to create an army of perfect Aryan children. Fully indoctrinated with Nazi propaganda since birth, Max has become a mascot of sorts for the Lebensborn program. As such, he acts as bait for the abduction of Polish children who could pass as Aryan. Once he is no longer viable bait, he is enrolled at the Kalish school to facilitate the Germinization of the abductees. There he meets Lukas, a rebellious abductee who is harboring a dangerous secret – he is actually Jewish. Max has to decide whether to out his new friend as a Jew, or that maybe, just maybe, the Führer’s teachings are wrong. <br /><br /><br />This book sheds a light on the Lebensborn program, one of the lesser known atrocities of the Third Reich. Due to the grim subject matter and the author’s refusal to pull any punches in regards to the graphic brutality of life under Nazi rule, this is a story best suited to mature readers. The splitting of the book into parts helps illustrate the rise and fall of Nazi Germany, as well as the fall of everything Max was raised to believe in. The author uses an infant narrator as a tool to deliberately cultivate a sense of unease in the reader, as it really pushes home the many crimes against humanity committed by the Nazis. After all, what kind of monsters can treat children, the most vulnerable among us, in such a way? -HF<br /><br />Click here to place a hold on <a href="http://osw.ent.sirsi.net/client/en_US/default/search/detailnonmodal/ent:$002f$002fSD_ILS$002f0$002fSD_ILS:258019/email?qu=max&amp;qf=ITEMCAT2%09Audience+Level%091%3AYA%09Young+Adult&amp;d=ent%3A%2F%2FSD_ILS%2F0%2FSD_ILS%3A258019~ILS~1" rel="nofollow noopener">

  <i>Salt to the Sea</i>

<div id="review_3168361113" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3168361113" />
    <a title="Julia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/108308818-julia"><img alt="Julia" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3168361113?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julia" href="/user/show/108308818-julia">Julia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3168361113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6347827998812993556">This book was a historical fiction novel about Hitler's Youth. The book was told through the perspective of a child, Max, and he was of the "superior Aryan race". Max lives at the hospital he was born in until he is four years old (he is part of the Lebensborn program). When he is four years old, he is moved out of the city where he was born to help the Nazis find Polish children that they could take and Germanize. After a few years of this, Max is moved to a school in Kalish, where he begins to</span>
  <span id="freeText6347827998812993556" style="display:none">This book was a historical fiction novel about Hitler's Youth. The book was told through the perspective of a child, Max, and he was of the "superior Aryan race". Max lives at the hospital he was born in until he is four years old (he is part of the Lebensborn program). When he is four years old, he is moved out of the city where he was born to help the Nazis find Polish children that they could take and Germanize. After a few years of this, Max is moved to a school in Kalish, where he begins to go through training in order to fight in the war when he is old enough, or suddenly needed. Max and Lucas (Max's "friend"), eventually leave Kalish to leave the war-torn area, looking for a new place to live where things are calmer, but Lucas ends up getting shot by a Russian soldier. I would use this book in a twelfth grade classroom to create awareness about Hitler's use and the experiences youth had to go through while the war was going on, from the Germans' perspective. However, I advise teachers to be careful before assigning this book because there are many graphic details and scenes in this book that may not be appropriate for a high school audience. </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('civflf5UEiYcH6FkxjdsCeWu7KZfiLvLMBhrYFnkhuwkP1KOmQpiPfU6G21i3+7msR7cUy7Gw08nRftqP9zO/w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('J8dDRIkvZ9O2/rWRc46/8qME3mNsPw4C3LQ3EFR0HUFx085f7nEXyF/bD5jXZj0d97Tulh1xdobL6acaMkxVUg==')})
  }

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;It is rubbish and that’s exactly why we have to burn it. It’s fun seeing the books fall to pieces as they land.
